Petah Tikva, meaning "Opening of Hope", is a city in Israel. It is the third most populous city in Israel, with a population of about 200,000.  Petah Tikva is located on the Sharon Plain, about 40 km (25 mi) north of Tel Aviv, and is a suburb of Tel Aviv, which lies to its south.  The city was founded in 1882 by a group of Russian Jews who had settled in the area during the 1860s. The name was chosen by a group of the settlers, who considered it to be symbolic of the new Jewish settlement.  Petah Tikva was incorporated as a city in 1949.  The main industries are agriculture and light industry.  It is also home to the Petah Tikva Museum of Art and the Israeli Opera.  The city is served by the Petah Tikva railway station, which is on the Tel Aviv-Rishon Lezion railway.  The city is the home of the Petah Tikva Hapoel F.C. football club, which plays in the Israeli Premier League. It was formerly the home of the Hapoel Petah Tikva F.C. team, which played in the Israeli State League.

Alan B. Miller Hall is an academic building at the College of William and Mary in Williamsburg, Virginia. It is the largest academic building on the campus, and is located between the Collegiate Church and the Thomas Jefferson Building. It was designed by Robert A. M. Stern of the architecture firm Skidmore, Owings and Merrill, and opened on March 30, 2007. It was named for Alan B. Miller, a former dean of the College of William and Mary, and was built as part of a $200 million renovation of the college's central campus. Stacy Katzman is an English-language film directed by Jared Hess, written by Hess and Michael Bacall, and starring Kristen Wiig, Bill Hader, Paul Dano, and James Caan. The film was released on August 11, 2009, in the United States by Roadside Attractions and Lionsgate, and grossed $25 million worldwide.  The film is based on the true story of the kidnapping of John Paul Getty III, grandson of the oil tycoon J. Paul Getty, in Rome, Italy in 1973. The film focuses on the efforts of his mother, Gail Harris (Wiig), to convince the wealthy Getty family to pay the ransom.  Hess, Bacall, and Wiig had worked together on the short film The Wackness (2008), which Bacall co-wrote. Hess and Wiig also collaborated on a second short film, Fun Size (2008), and were planning to do another project together. In May 2008, Wiig and Hess announced that they were writing a feature film, which they would direct and star in. Wiig also announced that she was in talks to produce and star in the film with Hess, Bacall, and Scott Rudin. In July 2008, it was announced that the film would be titled Super Troopers and would be produced by Rudin, Wiig, and Hess.  The film was shot in Rome, Italy, and in the Los Angeles area. Production began on August 25, 2008, and was completed on November 16, 2008.  The film was released on August 11, 2009, in the United States. It received mixed reviews from critics, but was a commercial success, grossing $25 million worldwide.  In 2010, Hess said he would make a sequel to Super Troopers. He said that the script was finished, and that it would be set in the 1990s.  The film was originally titled The Troopers, a reference to the 1967 film The Dirty Dozen, and the Super Troopers comic book series. The title was changed to Super Troopers because it was thought that people would not understand the reference to The Dirty Dozen.

Death on a Factory Farm was a television documentary miniseries, directed by Tom Simon, that aired on HBO in 1999. It is based on the book of the same name by Barbara Ehrenreich. It was executive-produced by Tom Simon, and produced by Simon and Geof Bartz. The series is a documentary about the death of three farm workers, and their families, who were poisoned by pesticides on a farm in the Philippines. The series was released on DVD in 2000.  Death on a Factory Farm was nominated for an Emmy Award in the category of Outstanding Documentary or Nonfiction Special, and received a Peabody Award for the same category.  The documentary was broadcast on HBO on January 5, 1999.  Death on a Factory Farm was the first film by Tom Simon, who previously worked as an executive for HBO, and the first film to be released by his production company, Tom Simon Productions.  Death on a Factory Farm was filmed in the Philippines and at the home of Barbara Ehrenreich in the United States. The film is narrated by Barbara Ehrenreich.  The documentary focuses on the death of three farm workers, and their families, who were poisoned by pesticides on a farm in the Philippines. It covers the aftermath of the death of the three farm workers, and the effects that their death had on their families, and the workers at the farm.  The documentary also focuses on the work of the United States Agency for International Development (USAID) in the Philippines, and the problems that the agency has in trying to provide aid to the country.  The documentary was well received by critics, and has received several awards. Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport is the main airport of Spain, located in the city of Madrid, and is the principal hub for Spanish flag carrier Iberia. It is located approximately 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) north of downtown Madrid, and is the second busiest airport in Spain, after Barcelona-El Prat Airport, and the sixth busiest in Europe in terms of passenger traffic. It is also one of the largest airports in the world, by area. It is located in the municipality of Alcobendas in the autonomous community of Madrid, Spain. The airport is owned by the Spanish government and is operated by the state-owned company Aena. It is the main hub for the Spanish flag carrier Iberia. It is also the main base for Air Europa, Air Nostrum, Iberia Express, and Vueling Airlines. The airport was opened on 12 December 1928 as a military airfield, Adolfo Suárez Madrid-Barajas Airport. It was opened to civilian traffic on 1 January 1931, and was renamed Cuatro Vientos Airport until the name was changed again on 3 May 1946. The current name was adopted on 27 March 1983, after the death of former Spanish President Adolfo Suárez. The airport has two runways: the main runway, 07L/25R, is 3,200 metres (10,500 ft) long and can handle aircraft up to the Airbus A380, Boeing 747-8, and Boeing 777-300ER; and the secondary runway, 07R/25L, is 2,500 metres (8,200 ft) long and can handle aircraft up to the Boeing 747-400, Boeing 747-400F, and Boeing 747-8F. The airport has three terminals: T1, T2 and T3. Terminal 4 was closed on 1 January 2012, and Terminal T4S was opened on 18 May 2011. In April 2018, it was announced that Terminal 4 would be reopened in 2026, and that the airport will have six terminals. The airport has two passenger terminals, Terminal 1 and Terminal 2. Terminal 3 was opened in March 2006, and is designed to handle around 40 million passengers per year. In 2018, the airport handled more than 61 million passengers. The airport also has a cargo terminal, which handles around 600,000 tonnes of cargo a year. In 2011, the airport handled 9,927,862 tonnes of cargo. Bananaman, starring Bill Oddie, is a British comedy television series created by Oddie and Terry Nation. It ran on BBC Two from 1983 to 1986, and was revived for one series in 1990. It was a major influence on the later US animated series The Simpsons. The programme is about a banana named Bananaman, who lives in a banana house in a garden and fights crime with his best friend, a black cat named Screwball. The series was produced by Nation's company, Triggerfish Animation, and was the first British television programme to be animated entirely on computers. The series is a satire on crime shows such as Police Surgeon, and has been described as "a cross between Doctor Who and The Benny Hill Show." The first series aired from October to December 1983. The second series was broadcast in 1984 and the third in 1985. The series was revived in 1990 and ran for one series. The theme tune was performed by the rock band The Beat. The programme was popular in the UK, and was voted Best TV Comedy at the British Comedy Awards in 1984 and 1985. The first series was nominated for an International Emmy Award in 1984, and the programme was the first British programme to be broadcast in the United States. The programme was also popular in Australia, and was broadcast in New Zealand. The programme is notable for its influence on The Simpsons, as producer Matt Groening was a fan of the show. In 2014, the BBC launched a new animated series, The Krankies, based on the Bananaman characters.

Acharya Institute of Technology was established in the year 1985 by the Visvesvaraya Technological University Act No. 25 of 1985 of the Karnataka State Legislature, which came into force on 1st July, 1986. Acharya Institute of Technology is a member of the Association of Indian Universities. The Institute is recognized by the All India Council for Technical Education (AICTE) and the Government of Karnataka. The City Manager is the chief administrative officer and serves as the Chief Executive Officer of the City of Ciudad Ayala. The City Manager is responsible for the general management of the City of Ciudad Ayala. The City Manager is responsible for the day-to-day operations of the City and the efficient administration of City government. The City Manager is responsible for the management of City employees, City finances, City facilities and City services. The City Manager is responsible for the development and implementation of policies, plans and programs. The City Manager works with the City Council, City staff, City departments, the City Attorney and the community to ensure that the City operates in a fiscally responsible manner and provides the highest quality of City services and facilities to its citizens. The City Manager is the administrative head of the City, and as such, has the authority to hire, suspend, fire, or otherwise discipline City employees. The City Manager has the authority to appoint the City's Executive Director, City Clerk, City Treasurer and City Attorney. The City Manager is also responsible for the implementation of the City's legislative program. The Honeymoon Killers are an American band from Portland, Oregon. They formed in 1984 and have released five albums. Their sound is characterized by heavy distorted guitars, fuzz bass, and drums. They have been described as a punk rock band, but their music is often also compared to heavy metal, noise rock, and hardcore punk. The band is named after a line in the song "Dark Side of the Moon" by Pink Floyd. The song was one of their favorites, and they liked the way the line "...keep on turning me on" was repeated in the song. The name was suggested by a friend of the band's guitarist, Sean Clancy. The band is led by vocalist/bassist Sean Clancy, who also plays guitar and keyboards. Sean Clancy is the only original member of the band, and he is the only member who has been with the band since its inception. The rest of the band has changed over the years, but Sean Clancy has remained the only constant. The band has released five studio albums. Their debut album, Dime, was released in 1985 and produced by Bob Egan, who was also a member of The Weirdos. It was re-released in 2006 by the band's own label, Fat Possum Records. The band's second album, Big Bang, was released in 1986. It was also produced by Bob Egan. It was re-released by Fat Possum Records in 2006. The band's third album, Hoover, was released in 1988. It was produced by Steve Albini. It was re-released by Fat Possum Records in 2006. The band's fourth album, The Big Black and the Blue, was released in 1991. Black metal music is a genre of extreme metal music that originated in Norway in the early 1980s. The earliest Norwegian black metal bands were influenced by earlier extreme metal bands such as Venom, Hellhammer and Celtic Frost. The genre is characterized by blast beats, tremolo picking, extreme tempo and volume, and lyrics dealing with death, occultism, satanism, and anti-Christianity. Black metal has been described as a mix of doom metal and thrash metal. The genre is often associated with the subculture of the black metal scene, which is characterized by the wearing of corpse paint and the use of pentagrams and inverted crosses as symbols. The genre has been subject to controversy, with critics such as musicologist Simon Reynolds and journalist Ann Cvetkovich accusing some black metal bands of promoting fascism, racism, and anti-Semitism. Aaron Turner is a British musician and record producer, best known as the vocalist and guitarist of the American black metal band Isis. Turner began his musical career in the early 1990s with his band, The Psychic Paramount, a group that would later change its name to Isis. He has also worked with other musicians, including the Norwegian black metal band Dimmu Borgir, the British punk rock band The Ruts, and the British experimental rock band Swans. Turner has been a prolific recording artist, releasing over 30 albums as both a solo artist and as a member of various bands. The president of the Chamber of Deputies is the head of the legislative branch of Mexico's federal government. The president is elected by the members of the Chamber of Deputies for a single, six-year term. The president of the Chamber of Deputies is the third in the line of succession to the presidency of Mexico, behind the president of Mexico and the president of the Senate.
